  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_119eaa1d-c993-4332-ba27-1164a8e9b8d1'

  <span id="freeText16887927748635124336" style="display:none"><b>The Secret Series continues in this dangerous and daring fourth adventure. </b><br /><br /> Cass finds herself alone and disoriented, a stranger in a dream-like, medieval world. Where is she? Who is she? With the help of a long-lost relative, she begins to uncover clues and secrets--piecing together her family's history as she fights her way back to the present world.<br /><br /> Meanwhile, back home, Cass is at the hospital in a deep coma. Max-Ernest knows she ate Time Travel Chocolate--and he's determined to find a cure. Can our expert hypochondriac diagnose Cass's condition before it's too late? And will he have what it takes to save the survivalist?</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1197641378" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15302518877254312602"> The book that I just finished is called This Isn't What it Looks Like by Pseudonymous Bosch. It’s about a girl name Cassandra, but everyone calls her Cass. Cass goes on wild mission to find the secret from the Jester. She uses a “Time Chocolate” to make her go back in time to know the secret. This makes her go into a coma, which makes Max-Ernest go and visit her in the PICU section. While Cass is in the coma, Max-Ernest finds some solution to help Cass come back to life. This adventure is an ex</span>
  <span id="freeText15302518877254312602" style="display:none"> The book that I just finished is called This Isn't What it Looks Like by Pseudonymous Bosch. It’s about a girl name Cassandra, but everyone calls her Cass. Cass goes on wild mission to find the secret from the Jester. She uses a “Time Chocolate” to make her go back in time to know the secret. This makes her go into a coma, which makes Max-Ernest go and visit her in the PICU section. While Cass is in the coma, Max-Ernest finds some solution to help Cass come back to life. This adventure is an experience to a whole new world, the past.<br /><br /> I like how the author contributes to the story because he is explaining the reasons the characters do the actions and words. The author is the third-person point of view, but he acts he is part of the story. I really like this book because it has many mysteries that have yet to be discovered. I also like how the villains are called the Midnight Sun because there is a backstory to the name of it. This is keeping me of suspense because the Midnight Sun are a pain to make-up devil plans. I also like this book because of the name of the characters are clues to the secret. In conclusion, I really like this book from all the mystery and the adventure </span>

<div id="review_501567628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/501567628" />
    <a title="Caitlin L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13862623-caitlin-l"><img alt="Caitlin L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352231666p2/13862623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/501567628?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin L" href="/user/show/13862623-caitlin-l">Caitlin L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer501567628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12443474527704912102"> I recently finished, "This Isn't What It Looks Like" by: Pseudonymous Bosch, the 4th book in the secret series. This book is told from two points of view, the survivalist girl, Cass and her trustworthy partner, Mas-Ernest. Cass ate a piece of Time Travel Chocolate and now she's been taken back to the medieval times of the Jester, her only known ancestor. Cass must find The Secret, it's her mission! Meanwhile, Max-Ernest is trying to get Cass out of her coma, before it's too late. <br/> This book is </span>
  <span id="freeText12443474527704912102" style="display:none"> I recently finished, "This Isn't What It Looks Like" by: Pseudonymous Bosch, the 4th book in the secret series. This book is told from two points of view, the survivalist girl, Cass and her trustworthy partner, Mas-Ernest. Cass ate a piece of Time Travel Chocolate and now she's been taken back to the medieval times of the Jester, her only known ancestor. Cass must find The Secret, it's her mission! Meanwhile, Max-Ernest is trying to get Cass out of her coma, before it's too late. <br /> This book is full of suspense, mystery, and a slight touch of humor. The characters aren't described very well because the author is trying to keep the characters identities a secret. I can kind of relate to Max-Ernest because he thought he knew how to bring Cass back but the remedy didn't work! I feel that way a lot, so close yet so far to getting to the right answer. Sometimes when I can't figure something out, it makes me want to rip my hair out! Bosch did a great job writing the plot, although sometimes it gets off track. He will often stop the story to tell us to tell the reader to stop reading now, or to tell us what he's doing. Overall, this book was amazingly written!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12443474527704912102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1372586337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372586337" />
    <a title="Rachael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28760393-rachael"><img alt="Rachael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420193026p2/28760393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1372586337?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachael" href="/user/show/28760393-rachael">Rachael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316076241" href="/book/show/10790443-this-isn-t-what-it-looks-like">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372586337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14087716840776873102">You can read my review on my blog here (& below):<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://elementaread.blogspot.co.uk/2015/08/review-this-isnt-what-it-looks-like-by.html'>http://elementaread.blogspot.co.uk/20...</a><br/><br/>THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS FOR THE PREVIOUS BOOKS IN THIS SERIES<br/><br/>'This Isn’t What it Looks Like' is the fourth book in the middle-grade ‘Secret Series’ by Pseudonymous Bosch. These books follow the adventures of three young members of the Terces Society, a secret organisation whose job it is to keep the Secret (to immortality) from getting into the wrong hands. On three previous occasions these children, C</span>
  <span id="freeText14087716840776873102" style="display:none">You can read my review on my blog here (&amp; below):<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://elementaread.blogspot.co.uk/2015/08/review-this-isnt-what-it-looks-like-by.html">http://elementaread.blogspot.co.uk/20...</a><br /><br />THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS FOR THE PREVIOUS BOOKS IN THIS SERIES<br /><br />'This Isn’t What it Looks Like' is the fourth book in the middle-grade ‘Secret Series’ by Pseudonymous Bosch. These books follow the adventures of three young members of the Terces Society, a secret organisation whose job it is to keep the Secret (to immortality) from getting into the wrong hands. On three previous occasions these children, Cassandra, Max-Ernest and Yo-Yogi, have thwarted the evil Midnight Sun's plans and kept the Secret safe.<br /><br />At the end of the previous book Cass has discovered that she is a decedent from the Jester, the original founder of the Terces Society, and that she is the Secret-Keeper. The only problem is, she doesn’t actually know the Secret. With the remains of Senor Hugo's extra strong time-travel-chocolate, Cass has gone back to medieval times to meet the Jester and find out what the Secret is.<br />Unfortunately for Cass, while her mind is in the past her body is still very much in the present and the adults believe she has fallen into a coma. She is in the hospital's Paediatric Intensive Care Unit and her distraught mother is unwilling to let Max-Ernest visit. The couple of times Max-Ernest has been close enough to Cass to try and give her the antidote and bring her back, it hasn’t worked.<br /><br />Meanwhile Cass meets a seer also named Cassandra who gives her some advice, and a useful double monocle which allows her to see far away and through solid objects. But the evil alchemist, and founder of the Midnight Sun, Lord Pharaoh finds Cass while she is searching for the Jester and ends up locking her in a cell with her ancestor. In the process he steals the double monocle and the last remaining piece of the time-travel-chocolate. Cass has now found what she was looking for, but will the Jester be able to help her uncover the Secret? And can Max-Ernest wake Cass up before it is too late?<br /><br />This really is such a great adventure series for both kids and adults alike! These books are a fantastic mix of mystery, action and adventure with a little time-travel and alchemy thrown in. The characters are fantastic and I especially like Cass, the survivalist, and Owen, the master of disguise.<br /><br />There were some great new characters introduced in this book too. I LOVED the Jester and Anastasia is a brilliant bad-ass bandit. Mr Cabbage Face, the homunculus for book two also makes a brief, but memorable appearance as his past-self. Ms Mauvais and Dr L don’t play such a big part in the book, but in their place we meet the horribly evil Lord Pharaoh.<br /><br />The story was so fast-paced and well written. I really enjoy this authors writing style, and I love the little footnotes and appendices. This book also has a fantastic little author interview at the back which was a fun read :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14087716840776873102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2768134-beth-g?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2768134-beth-g?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2768134-beth-g?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2768134-beth-g?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2768134-beth-g?shelf=books-for-kids">books-for-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2768134-beth-g?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141662917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18251806314607704686">The fourth book in the series that began with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1099301.The_Name_of_this_Book_is_Secret' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Name of This Book is Secret</a> picks up where the third volume left off. In the early chapters, narrator Bosch splits attention between two stories: one is about a girl who wakes up in what appears to be a medieval European village unable to remember who she is, where she is, how she got there, or why she happens to be invisible; the other is about Max-Ernest, who is desperately trying to awaken his friend Cass, who has been in a strange sort of com</span>
  <span id="freeText18251806314607704686" style="display:none">The fourth book in the series that began with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1099301.The_Name_of_this_Book_is_Secret" rel="nofollow noopener">The Name of This Book is Secret</a> picks up where the third volume left off. In the early chapters, narrator Bosch splits attention between two stories: one is about a girl who wakes up in what appears to be a medieval European village unable to remember who she is, where she is, how she got there, or why she happens to be invisible; the other is about Max-Ernest, who is desperately trying to awaken his friend Cass, who has been in a strange sort of coma since taking a dose of time-travel chocolate. The reader can quickly figure out how these two stories mesh (you've probably put it together just reading this review), and it's a relief when the two stories converge into one.<br /><br />There is a lot of silliness here, in the style of the writing as well as the plot. Cass and Max-Ernest remain the center ground for the reader amid the swirl of outrageous situations and goofy narration. Bosch reads much like Lemony Snicket, explaining things in footnotes and hinting at secrets never quite revealed. Several of these footnotes refer the reader back to previous installments in the series; jumping into the series with this book is definitely not recommended. A cliff-hanger ending (and the fact that our heroes still haven't uncovered The Secret) leaves readers anxiously anticipating the final volume, slated for publication in October 2011.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18251806314607704686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15882505538460728342">Summary: In this fourth installment of the Secret Series, Cass is stuck in the Medieval Ages on a mission to find the Secret (having learned she was the Secret Keeper) while Max-Ernest is on a desperate mission to bring her back. Complications arise when Max-Ernest's parents begin acting strangely, and an old classmate comes back, suspiciously different. Can Max-Ernest save Cass? Or will Cass forever be stuck in the Middle Ages?<br/><br/>My thoughts (Note: This review is for the whole series):<br/>I LOVE THE S</span>
  <span id="freeText15882505538460728342" style="display:none">Summary: In this fourth installment of the Secret Series, Cass is stuck in the Medieval Ages on a mission to find the Secret (having learned she was the Secret Keeper) while Max-Ernest is on a desperate mission to bring her back. Complications arise when Max-Ernest's parents begin acting strangely, and an old classmate comes back, suspiciously different. Can Max-Ernest save Cass? Or will Cass forever be stuck in the Middle Ages?<br /><br />My thoughts (Note: This review is for the whole series):<br />I LOVE THE SECRET SERIES!!! The plot for each book is interesting and each one is different. The characters are all believable, relatable, and have distinct personalities. The Appendices at the end of each book were cool too, as they usually contained activities, games, and some information. So I loved this series, and you should give it a try. Pseudonymous Bosch also has a book called Write this Book; a Do-it Yourself mystery, which is a sort of guide for young writers on how to write a mystery. It's not completely related to the Secret Series (there are, however, some references to it in Write This Book), but I still recommend reading the Secret Series first. Happy reading!</span>

  <u>Short and Simple Review</u>
</b><br />Other reviewers found this one to be lacking compared to the other books. I can see why because Cass is wondering in time, but unconscious in our time. Meanwhile, Max-Ernest is trying to figure out how to save her. This does sound a bit boring, but I actually really liked this one. It was actually my favorite one so far. I love time travel, so I liked seeing that come into play. It was also interesting seeing the history of the Midnight Sun and the Terces Society. The book also touches on how written history is not always accurate. Cass's character is really strong in this one, in fact, she becomes a stronger character with every book. The Secret is, of course, still secret, but Cass is close to figuring it out. Again, the narrator is fantastic, just like the last books in the series. </span>

<div id="review_2982164301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2982164301" />
    <a title="Avery Ethington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101574248-avery-ethington"><img alt="Avery Ethington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566329270p2/101574248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2982164301?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Avery Ethington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Avery Ethington" href="/user/show/101574248-avery-ethington">Avery Ethington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2982164301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2258284545802856073"> The book, This Isn’t What It Looks Like, by Pseudonymous Bosh, is a very excellent book and is told from two points of view by the main characters, Cassandra (Cass for short), and her best friend Max-Ernest. In the beginning of the book Cass “wakes up” and can’t remember who she is, where she came from, or how she got there. She later figures out that she is in a different time period, or more specifically, medieval times. Cass remembers that she is there to find the Jester, her great great gre</span>
  <span id="freeText2258284545802856073" style="display:none"> The book, This Isn’t What It Looks Like, by Pseudonymous Bosh, is a very excellent book and is told from two points of view by the main characters, Cassandra (Cass for short), and her best friend Max-Ernest. In the beginning of the book Cass “wakes up” and can’t remember who she is, where she came from, or how she got there. She later figures out that she is in a different time period, or more specifically, medieval times. Cass remembers that she is there to find the Jester, her great great great something grandfather, so that she can figure out the Secret from him. Meanwhile, in the real time, Max-Ernest is sitting beside real time Cass, who is in a coma. It is Max-Ernest’s job to wake her up from her chocolate-induced coma, but nothing seems to be working. As these two adventures unfold, they figure out that their so-called friends, might be their foes, and that nothing is what it looks like.<br /> I really liked this book because it is a page turner and keeps you on the edge of your seat. There is lots of adventure, mystery, and betrayal. When you least expect it, there is the ultimate plot twist. The characters often have to break the law, and do perilous stunts that seem impossible. This book will never let you down.<br /> I would recommend this book to anyone who is looking for either, something exciting to read, a mystery to read, or something mystical and exciting. This book may be harder for younger kids who are 9 or younger, because there are harder words, and the books contain 300 pages or more. If you are looking for a new series to be engrossed in, then this book is the right one for you. Beware though, you will definitely be so obsessed with this book, that you will read it nonstop and over and over and over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2258284545802856073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1659647387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1659647387" />
    <a title="Jun Wong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47266313-jun-wong"><img alt="Jun Wong" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1659647387?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jun Wong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jun Wong" href="/user/show/47266313-jun-wong">Jun Wong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1659647387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1330813764494427164">As Clear as a Crystal <br/><br/>The Author, Pseudonymous Bosch, of "This isn't What it Looks Like" has a writing style of comedy, but mixed with an aurora of mysteriousness. Pseudonymous Bosch keeps a shroud of mystery between his identity, along with many fourth wall breaks when he inserts his own dialogue, sort of like a commentary throughout the books. He talks to the readers, giving off a maniac vibe in my opinion, yet maintaining sanity. The writing of Bosch is clear as he manages to stay on track wi</span>
  <span id="freeText1330813764494427164" style="display:none">As Clear as a Crystal <br /><br />The Author, Pseudonymous Bosch, of "This isn't What it Looks Like" has a writing style of comedy, but mixed with an aurora of mysteriousness. Pseudonymous Bosch keeps a shroud of mystery between his identity, along with many fourth wall breaks when he inserts his own dialogue, sort of like a commentary throughout the books. He talks to the readers, giving off a maniac vibe in my opinion, yet maintaining sanity. The writing of Bosch is clear as he manages to stay on track with the Secret Series, continuing the story of the 2 young detectives, Cass and Max-Ernst, as their quest to uncover the unrecoverable secret hidden for nearly a century. He manages to balance out internal development with external development well, as he also works with two different parts as they eventually do converge on each other to create one full plot line, making everything make sense throughout. His choice of words as cynical and a bit Monty Python like, keeps the book entertaining and very interesting as it keeps the reader at the edge of their seats. <br /><br />Like Water in a Desert<br /><br />I found the author to be very entertaining and quite the personality. He managed to insert his own viewpoints of the book, giving us a new perspective of the book. He breaks the fourth wall many times, making the book much more enjoyable. I found that his writing style was very engrossing. He even added an intermission halfway through his book to “Requested a fifteen-minute break to restore his energy before writing what promises to be a very intense and emotional chapter.” He keeps things light and casual then diving into a story full of mystery. Readers will definitely like the new perspective the author includes in his books, as they give a fresh viewpoint on the things at hand, and helps with the massive storyline, giving the readers to take a step back and view the story through a different set of eyes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1330813764494427164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10307891401734259134" style="display:none">Originally posted @ <a href="http://bookwhales.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Whales</a><br><br>We are on the penultimate book of the Secret Series. :D<br>To tell you honestly I finished this books 3 weeks ago and I just forgot to make a review out of it. But finally here it is :D<br><br>Out of the 4 books I read the problem I have with this books is that maybe I got used to the writing style of the author and the magic is lost for me. The plot itself for this books is very important to the story since it explains a lot about the history of the Jester and Lord Pharaoh with the secret. But when I was reading it I can't help myself but be bored. Here are some of my speculations on why I was bored with this 4th book.<br><br>1. I read Book 1-4 continuously that the surprising element is lost in the way.<br>2. As I said earlier, I got used to the writing style and made the story a little bit predictable.<br>3. There were a lot of boring moments and I think its because the main characters are not together for the first time. (Since Cass was time travelling)<br>4. And then I think it also added that the main antagonist get no time or a little appearance in this book. <br><br>The only positive thing about this is that maybe finally Max-Earnest got a little bit backbone in this book.         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1462214769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14316261923416363152">I read this directly after reading the third one, which is not something I usually do. When I read a series I like to read two or more books in between so that I don’t feel the books get too same-y. But this time I really wanted to keep reading this mystery series seeing as the previous book ended on such a cliffhanger. <br/><br/>Our familiar trio of Cassandra, Max-Ernest and Yo-Yoji return in this book with some new characters in tow, like Daniel-Not-Danielle, the Glob, the Jester and Anastasia as well. </span>
  <span id="freeText14316261923416363152" style="display:none">I read this directly after reading the third one, which is not something I usually do. When I read a series I like to read two or more books in between so that I don’t feel the books get too same-y. But this time I really wanted to keep reading this mystery series seeing as the previous book ended on such a cliffhanger. <br /><br />Our familiar trio of Cassandra, Max-Ernest and Yo-Yoji return in this book with some new characters in tow, like Daniel-Not-Danielle, the Glob, the Jester and Anastasia as well. Cassandra is in grave danger, and Max-Ernest must save her before it’s too late. While Cass is racing through time, Max-Ernest is racing against it. Either way, the past and present (and even future) all play together to unlock bits of the mystery continued from the previous book.<br /><br />What I liked so much about this book was that it had a lot of focus from Max-Ernest’s perspective, even though we usually get to see more from Cassandra’s. This is why Max-Ernest became my favourite character. We get to see how much he cares for his friends, how much it hurts to be replaced and also how to deal with separated parents who seem to reattach themselves to each other. Aside from all this, Max-Ernest has his own quirks, like his illness and undying love for chocolate.<br /><br />I’m going to keep this fairly short because I don’t want to give away any major plot points. But go read this!<br /><br />This review and more can be found on Olivia's Catastrophe: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://olivia-savannah.blogspot.nl/2015/12/mini-reviews-two-middle-grade-favourites.html">http://olivia-savannah.blogspot.nl/20...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13690995440187804806">I really enjoyed this one! The previous novels in the series were good, but not real page-turners for me. But this one really hit the sweet spot in terms of pacing and plotting. I loved the setup with the negative chapters eventually hitting chapter zero. All the plot elements tied together very nicely. <br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Loved the idea of Max-Ernest being Pseudonymous Bosch. It would certainly explain why Pseudonymous Bosch can't help himself from adding in delightful but useless factoids in footno</span></span>
  <span id="freeText13690995440187804806" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this one! The previous novels in the series were good, but not real page-turners for me. But this one really hit the sweet spot in terms of pacing and plotting. I loved the setup with the negative chapters eventually hitting chapter zero. All the plot elements tied together very nicely. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Loved the idea of Max-Ernest being Pseudonymous Bosch. It would certainly explain why Pseudonymous Bosch can't help himself from adding in delightful but useless factoids in footnotes everywhere. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />This novel really ungrounds us from reality, going from what seems like exaggerated, but plausible, reality to the fantastical realm. It was weird at first, but with a little suspension of disbelief, I found it quite delightful. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Joker and Anastasia were pretty adorable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Speaking of excellent characters, the new Nuts Table ones were great. The little details, like Daniel-not-Danielle and back story of the Nuts Table really trigger my own not-so-fond memories of middle school.<br />I must say, too, that while the many footnotes and digressions (such as the emergency drill) can be a mite annoying sometimes, they are for the most part absolutely delightful and hilarious. I've always loved the appendices, too, and found it an excellent idea to have recipes/crafts/codes etc in the back from the book. Loved the book, and looking forwards to picking up the next one.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19899918-laura-phelps?shelf=to-give-to-lizzie-when-she-s-older">to-give-to-lizzie-when-she-s-older</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer978475925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2843772297366878806">In this fourth installment of the secret series, Cass and Max-Earnest are separated by time and place... in a way. Cass is stuck in the past searching for The Secret, but she's also in a coma in the present, and it's Max-Earnest's job to save her. For whatever reason, though, he can't.<br/><br/>I read the first three books of this series, The Name of the Book is Secret, If You're Reading This, It's Too Late, and This Book Is Not Good For You, in middle school, and I thrilled when I saw this at the store. </span>
  <span id="freeText2843772297366878806" style="display:none">In this fourth installment of the secret series, Cass and Max-Earnest are separated by time and place... in a way. Cass is stuck in the past searching for The Secret, but she's also in a coma in the present, and it's Max-Earnest's job to save her. For whatever reason, though, he can't.<br /><br />I read the first three books of this series, The Name of the Book is Secret, If You're Reading This, It's Too Late, and This Book Is Not Good For You, in middle school, and I thrilled when I saw this at the store. I picked it (along with the next book, You Have To Stop This) up and am so glad I did! I was a bit concerned that it was the kind of book is good when you're thirteen, but not when you're older, but I was so wrong. It's still just as funny, just as quirky (in a GOOD way), and just as clever.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to any child or adult, but I'd specifically like to recommend this to anyone who enjoys Welcome To Nightvale. It's pretty different, but I think anyone who likes one would like the other. They're both humorously dark and just.... weird. But not oh-look-how-weird-I-am-aren't-I-cool? Just different, refreshing, hilarious, wonderful. I mean, the author's pen name is Pseudonymous Bosch. The books tell you not to read them.You just can't go wrong with that!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6463869615370482096">Hmm..well, let me just suggest something. If you really want to read this book, go and buy the paperback, DO NOT GET IT ON KINDLE/NOOK. That was my mistake. There were some things that you would need to go to the back of the book, or to the beginning, and it was annoying to have to find what you were looking for (i.e. Yo-Yoji's email to Max-Ernest) tons of times (and not to mention, it's can be quite slow) when if you just got the paperback, you could flip to the back of the book. And also, when</span>
  <span id="freeText6463869615370482096" style="display:none">Hmm..well, let me just suggest something. If you really want to read this book, go and buy the paperback, DO NOT GET IT ON KINDLE/NOOK. That was my mistake. There were some things that you would need to go to the back of the book, or to the beginning, and it was annoying to have to find what you were looking for (i.e. Yo-Yoji's email to Max-Ernest) tons of times (and not to mention, it's can be quite slow) when if you just got the paperback, you could flip to the back of the book. And also, when there were those notes he leaves with the *, you had to click on them to show the note, which was also a little annoying as some of them were pointless.<br />Though, that's my fault for buying it on the Kindle, or since I'm quite lazy.:p<br />As for the story, it was pretty good! Probably the best out of the 4 so far, and unlike the others this one I couldn't predict the ending or how things would turn out.<br />Not much to say about this book, actually, as I didn't have any major complaints (other than the pointless * notes) and I do like his writing a lot. It's creative, just at times can be annoying.<br />So, all in all, a solid 4/5 stars.<br />(Well..ok. Maybe not solid..maybe like a 4.3? Haha.)</span>

Max-Ernest knows that Cass ate the time-travel chocolate, but he doesn't know how to get her back in to the present.   <span id="freeText16115956549918876740" style="display:none">In this fourth installment of The Secret Series, Cass is in a coma in a hospital and Max-Ernest is alone since Yo-Yoji is in Japan. Max-Ernest knows that Cass ate the time-travel chocolate, but he doesn't know how to get her back in to the present. Meanwhile, Cass is in a medieval time, with no memory of anything from before she appeared in this new place, searching for her ancestor, The Jester. She is invisible and is armed with an odd double-monocle from a Seer named Cassandra (who goes by Clara). As Cass' memory returns and she learns more about The Jester and Cabbage face the homunculus, she runs into Lord Pharaoh.... the founder of the Midnight Sun! Now that Cass has found the Jester, can she figure out the secret she's looking for? Can Max-Ernest bring Cass back in time? This book makes the series even better! If you've read the other three Secret Series books, don't stop now!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ecCM/GIxR6BATBfmqkyArlK0T1aIJK3+NWMcB/H0lu4zciru+WLiaMnA+BPPdKisMw8XUrm46EE6z+FiUkxNOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H5iwBiiK0jSYw3osvD/AsSuTVpf0z3JGmLceZENDplxVKhYUs9l3/BFPldnZB+izSigOk8VTN/mXG+MB4Pt9iA==')})
  }
